<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Foxy_Brown_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Foxy Brown (disambiguation)">Foxy Brown (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Partner(s)</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Kurupt" title="Kurupt">Kurupt</a><br /> (1997–1999)<br /><a href="/wiki/Spragga_Benz" title="Spragga Benz">Spragga Benz</a> <br />(2001–2003)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data">1</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Relatives</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Clark_Kent_(producer)" title="Clark Kent (producer)">Clark Kent</a> (cousin)<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div>
<p><b>Inga DeCarlo Fung Marchand</b> (born September 6, 1978),<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup> better known by her stage name <b>Foxy Brown</b>, is an American rapper.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> After signing to <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam</a> in 1996, she released her debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Ill_Na_Na" title="Ill Na Na">Ill Na Na</a></i>, later that year on November 19, 1996. The album was certified platinum by the RIAA and has sold over 7 million copies worldwide. She was also part of the hip hop supergroup <a href="/wiki/The_Firm_(hip_hop_group)" title="The Firm (hip hop group)">the Firm</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/AZ_(rapper)" title="AZ (rapper)">AZ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cormega" title="Cormega">Cormega</a> (who was later replaced by <a href="/wiki/Nature_(rapper)" title="Nature (rapper)">Nature</a>). <a href="/wiki/The_Album_(The_Firm_album)" title="The Album (The Firm album)">The Firm's sole album</a> arrived in 1997 and was released by <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a>. In 1999, her second album <i><a href="/wiki/Chyna_Doll_(album)" title="Chyna Doll (album)">Chyna Doll</a></i>, debuted at the top of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, making her the second female rapper to top the chart after <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a> in 1998.
</p><p>Her third album <i><a href="/wiki/Broken_Silence_(Foxy_Brown_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Broken Silence (Foxy Brown album)">Broken Silence</a></i>, was released in 2001, which featured the <a href="/wiki/Grammy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy">Grammy</a>-nominated track "Na Na Be Like".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, she left Def Jam and canceled the release of her <i>Ill Na Na 2</i> album, but returned in 2005 once <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, then the label's president and CEO, signed her again to begin work on another unreleased album titled <i>Black Roses</i>. Her <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Don_Diva" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Don Diva">Brooklyn Don Diva</a></i> was released in May 2008, and her <a href="/wiki/Visual_album" title="Visual album">visual album</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/King_Soon_Come_(Foxy_Brown_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="King Soon Come (Foxy Brown album)">King Soon Come</a></i>, was slated for 2019 release but has been delayed indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-Winslow_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Winslow-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Madden_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Madden-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Marchand is a <a href="/wiki/Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian_Americans" title="Trinidadian and Tobagonian Americans">Trinidadian-American</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dougla" class="mw-redirect" title="Dougla">Dougla</a> (mixed <a href="/wiki/Afro-Trinidadians_and_Tobagonians" title="Afro-Trinidadians and Tobagonians">Afro-Trinidadian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indo-Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian" title="Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonian">Indo-Trinidadian</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Trinidadians_and_Tobagonians" title="Chinese Trinidadians and Tobagonians">Chinese-Trinidadian</a> descent.<sup id="cite_ref-outspoken_4_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outspoken_4-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> She and her two older brothers grew up in <a href="/wiki/Park_Slope" title="Park Slope">Park Slope</a>, a <a href="/wiki/American_middle_class" title="American middle class">middle-class</a> neighborhood in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>. Her parents divorced when she was four, and her family  moved in with her maternal grandfather.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopedia.com_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopedia.com-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> She later attended  <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_College_Academy" title="Brooklyn College Academy">Brooklyn College Academy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopedia.com_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopedia.com-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1994.E2.80.931996:_Early_career"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994–1996:_Early_career">1994–1996: Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1994–1996: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While still a teenager, Brown won a talent contest in the Park Slope neighborhood of Brooklyn, New York. Members of the production team <a href="/wiki/Trackmasters" title="Trackmasters">Trackmasters</a> who were working on <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Smith_(album)" title="Mr. Smith (album)">Mr. Smith</a></i> album were in attendance that night and were impressed enough to invite Brown to rap on "<a href="/wiki/I_Shot_Ya" title="I Shot Ya">I Shot Ya</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> She followed this debut with appearances on several <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">RIAA platinum and gold singles</a> from other artists, including remixes of songs "You're Makin' Me High" by <a href="/wiki/Toni_Braxton" title="Toni Braxton">Toni Braxton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Brown was also featured on the soundtrack to the 1996 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Nutty_Professor_(1996_film)" title="The Nutty Professor (1996 film)">The Nutty Professor</a></i>, on the songs "<a href="/wiki/Touch_Me,_Tease_Me" title="Touch Me, Tease Me">Touch Me, Tease Me</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Case_(singer)" title="Case (singer)">Case</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_No_Nigga" title="Ain&#39;t No Nigga">Ain't No Nigga</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> She became an instant sensation due to being very talented and rapping provocatively at such a young age. The immediate success led to a label bidding war at the beginning of 1996, and in March, <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Def Jam Records">Def Jam Records</a> won and added the then 17-year-old rapper to their roster.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1996.E2.80.931997:_Ill_Na_Na_and_The_Firm"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996–1997:_Ill_Na_Na_and_The_Firm">1996–1997: <i>Ill Na Na</i> and The Firm</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1996–1997: Ill Na Na and The Firm">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1996, Brown released her debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Ill_Na_Na" title="Ill Na Na">Ill Na Na</a></i> to strong sales. The album sold over 128,000<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> copies in the first week, and debuted at No. 7 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 album charts.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The album was heavily produced by Trackmasters, and featured guest appearances from Jay-Z, <a href="/wiki/Blackstreet" title="Blackstreet">Blackstreet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Method_Man" title="Method Man">Method Man</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kid_Capri" title="Kid Capri">Kid Capri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The album was <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">platinum</a> and launched two hit singles: "<a href="/wiki/Get_Me_Home_(song)" title="Get Me Home (song)">Get Me Home</a>" (featuring Blackstreet) and "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_(Foxy_Brown_song)" title="I&#39;ll Be (Foxy Brown song)">I'll Be</a>" (featuring Jay-Z).<sup id="cite_ref-single_charts_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-single_charts-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the release of <i>Ill Na Na</i>, Brown joined fellow New York-based hip hop artists, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/AZ_(rapper)" title="AZ (rapper)">AZ</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cormega" title="Cormega">Cormega</a> (later replaced by <a href="/wiki/Nature_(rapper)" title="Nature (rapper)">Nature</a>) to form the <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a> known as <a href="/wiki/The_Firm_(hip_hop_group)" title="The Firm (hip hop group)">The Firm</a>. The album was released via <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Aftermath Records">Aftermath Records</a> and was produced and recorded by the collective team of <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Trackmasters" class="mw-redirect" title="The Trackmasters">the Trackmasters</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Stoute" title="Steve Stoute">Steve "Commissioner" Stoute</a>, then of <a href="/wiki/Violator_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Violator Entertainment">Violator Entertainment</a>. An early form of The Firm appeared on "Affirmative Action" from Nas' second album <i><a href="/wiki/It_Was_Written" title="It Was Written">It Was Written</a></i>. A remix of the song and several group <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyles</a> were on the album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Album_(The_Firm_album)" title="The Album (The Firm album)">Nas, Foxy Brown, AZ, and Nature Present The Firm: The Album</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-firm_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firm-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The album entered the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> album chart at No. 1.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Firm_–_Billboard_Albums_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Firm_–_Billboard_Albums-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 1997, she joined the <a href="/wiki/Spring_break" title="Spring break">spring break</a> festivities hosted by MTV in Panama City, Florida, among other performers including rapper <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, pop group <a href="/wiki/The_Spice_Girls" class="mw-redirect" title="The Spice Girls">The Spice Girls</a>, and rock band <a href="/wiki/Stone_Temple_Pilots" title="Stone Temple Pilots">Stone Temple Pilots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_News_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_News-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Later, she joined the Smokin' Grooves tour hosted by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Blues" title="House of Blues">House of Blues</a> with the headlining rap group <a href="/wiki/Cypress_Hill" title="Cypress Hill">Cypress Hill</a>, along with other performers like <a href="/wiki/Erykah_Badu" title="Erykah Badu">Erykah Badu</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a>, <a href="/wiki/OutKast" class="mw-redirect" title="OutKast">OutKast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Pharcyde" title="The Pharcyde">The Pharcyde</a>, the tour set to begin in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, Massachusetts, in the summer of 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-mtv.com_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv.com-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> However, after missing several dates in the tour, she left it.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1998.E2.80.931999:_Chyna_Doll"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998–1999:_Chyna_Doll">1998–1999: <i>Chyna Doll</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1998–1999: Chyna Doll">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Chyna_Doll_(album)" title="Chyna Doll (album)">Chyna Doll</a></i> was released in January 1999 and debuted at No. 1 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 Album chart,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> selling 173,000 copies in its opening week,<sup id="cite_ref-Boehlert_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boehlert-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> making her the second female rapper to accomplish this feat after Lauryn Hill.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> However, its sales quickly declined in later weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-Promis_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Promis-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> <i>Chyna Doll</i> has been certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_Certification" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA Certification">platinum</a> after surpassing one million copies sold in shipments.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.932003:_Broken_Silence_and_Ill_Na_Na_2:_The_Fever"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000–2003:_Broken_Silence_and_Ill_Na_Na_2:_The_Fever">2000–2003: <i>Broken Silence</i> and <i>Ill Na Na 2: The Fever</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2000–2003: Broken Silence and Ill Na Na 2: The Fever">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2001, Brown released <i><a href="/wiki/Broken_Silence_(Foxy_Brown_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Broken Silence (Foxy Brown album)">Broken Silence</a></i>. The single  "BK Anthem" showcased Brown's "street" image and giving a tribute to her hometown, Brooklyn, and to famous rappers such as <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a> and Jay-Z. The first single from the album was "<a href="/wiki/Oh_Yeah_(Foxy_Brown_song)" title="Oh Yeah (Foxy Brown song)">Oh Yeah</a>", which featured her then-boyfriend, Jamaican <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Spragga_Benz" title="Spragga Benz">Spragga Benz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Spragga_Benz_allmusic_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spragga_Benz_allmusic-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The track "Na Na Be Like" was produced by Kenya Fame Flames Miller and Nokio from <a href="/wiki/Dru_Hill" title="Dru Hill">Dru Hill</a>. The song "Candy", which featured guest vocals from <a href="/wiki/Kelis" title="Kelis">Kelis</a>, was never officially released as a single, but was hugely successful on the radio; it managed to chart at 48 on the R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Singles &amp; Track Chart and number 10 on the Rap charts". Na Na Be Like" was also on the <i>Blue Streak Soundtrack</i>.
</p><p>The album debuted on the Billboard Charts at No. 5, selling 130,000 units its first week. Like previous albums, <i>Broken Silence</i> also sold over 500,000 records and was certified <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Music recording sales certification">gold</a> by the <a href="/wiki/RIAA" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA">RIAA</a>.
</p><p>In the same year, Brown recorded a song for the action-comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Rush_Hour_2" title="Rush Hour 2">Rush Hour 2</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rush_Hour_2_(soundtrack)" title="Rush Hour 2 (soundtrack)">Blow My Whistle</a></i>, which is a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Japanese-American" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese-American">Japanese-American</a> singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Hikaru_Utada" title="Hikaru Utada">Hikaru Utada</a>, and was written by Utada herself alongside <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chad_Hugo" title="Chad Hugo">Chad Hugo</a>. The song is included on Def Jam's <i><a href="/wiki/Rush_Hour_2_(soundtrack)" title="Rush Hour 2 (soundtrack)">Rush Hour 2 Soundtrack</a></i>, which peaked the 11th spot on both the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> and also the first on the <a href="/wiki/Top_Soundtracks" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Soundtracks">Top Soundtracks</a>. "Blow My Whistle" was produced by <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rush_Hour_2_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rush_Hour_2-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2002, Brown returned to the music scene with her single "<a href="/wiki/Stylin%27" title="Stylin&#39;">Stylin'</a>", whose remix featured rappers <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(rapper)" title="Birdman (rapper)">Birdman</a>, her brother Gavin, <a href="/wiki/Loon_(rapper)" title="Loon (rapper)">Loon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/N.O.R.E." title="N.O.R.E.">N.O.R.E.</a> It was to be the first single from her upcoming album <i><a href="/wiki/Ill_Na_Na_2:_The_Fever" title="Ill Na Na 2: The Fever">Ill Na Na 2: The Fever</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The next year, she was featured on <a href="/wiki/DJ_Kayslay" class="mw-redirect" title="DJ Kayslay">DJ Kayslay</a>'s single "Too Much for Me" from his <i>Street Sweeper's Volume One Mixtape</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> She also appeared on <a href="/wiki/Luther_Vandross" title="Luther Vandross">Luther Vandross</a>' final studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Dance_with_My_Father_(album)_(redirect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dance with My Father (album) (redirect)">Dance with My Father</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jeffries_2003_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeffries_2003-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> That April, Brown appeared on popular New York radio DJ <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Williams_(radio_hostess)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wendy Williams (radio hostess)">Wendy Williams</a>' radio show, and revealed the details of her relationships with <a href="/wiki/Lyor_Cohen" title="Lyor Cohen">Lyor Cohen</a>, president of <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a> at the time, and <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean "P. Diddy" Combs</a>. Brown accused both of illegally trading her recording masters. She also announced that Cohen had cancelled promotion for her fourth album <i>Ill Na Na 2: The Fever</i> over personal disagreements.<sup id="cite_ref-Promotion_Cancelled_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Promotion_Cancelled-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Therefore, "Stylin'" was released on the compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Source (magazine)">The Source</a> Presents: Hip Hop Hits Vol. 6</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kellman_2002_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kellman_2002-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2004.E2.80.932008:_Black_Roses_and_Brooklyn.27s_Don_Diva"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2004–2008:_Black_Roses_and_Brooklyn's_Don_Diva">2004–2008: <i>Black Roses</i> and <i>Brooklyn's Don Diva</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2004–2008: Black Roses and Brooklyn&#039;s Don Diva">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Upon leaving Def Jam Recordings after her disappointment in the cancelled promotion of her studio album, <i>Ill Na Na 2: The Fever</i>, Brown began recording in late 2004. Months later, she reunited with Jay-Z, performing dates on the <a href="/wiki/Unfinished_Business_(Jay-Z_and_R._Kelly_album)#Best_of_Both_Worlds_Tour_(Jay-Z_and_R._Kelly)" title="Unfinished Business (Jay-Z and R. Kelly album)">Best of Both Worlds Tour</a>. After signing back to Def Jam under his regime, Brown and Jay-Z began work on <i>Black Roses</i> with production by <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trackmasters" title="Trackmasters">Trackmasters</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Kelly_(producer)" title="Dave Kelly (producer)">Dave Kelly</a>. Brown confirmed guest appearances by <a href="/wiki/Barrington_Levy" title="Barrington Levy">Barrington Levy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dido_(singer)" title="Dido (singer)">Dido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luther_Vandross" title="Luther Vandross">Luther Vandross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mos_Def" title="Mos Def">Mos Def</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baby_Cham" class="mw-redirect" title="Baby Cham">Baby Cham</a>, Spragga Benz, <a href="/wiki/Shyne" title="Shyne">Shyne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Daddy_Kane" title="Big Daddy Kane">Big Daddy Kane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rakim" title="Rakim">Rakim</a>, <a href="/wiki/KRS-One" title="KRS-One">KRS-One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roxanne_Shante" title="Roxanne Shante">Roxanne Shante</a>, and Jay-Z, although it was uncertain whether all would make the final cut for the album.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2004, Brown announced that the title for her upcoming album would be <i>Black Roses</i>, explaining, "My best friend <a href="/wiki/Barrington_Levy" title="Barrington Levy">Barrington Levy</a> has a song called "Black Roses." He's been traveling all over the world and never seen a black rose in no other garden. When he found his black rose, he knew that shit was special. Y'all niggas can have all the female rappers in the world, but there's only one black rose. I feel that's me."<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Brown also announced that she would be the first artist signed to Jay-Z's upcoming imprint record label <a href="/wiki/S._Carter_Records" title="S. Carter Records">S. Carter Records</a>. Rather than launching the imprint, though, Jay-Z became the new president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Def Jam Records">Def Jam Records</a>, where he signed Brown as one of the first artists on his new roster.<sup id="cite_ref-SOHH_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOHH-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On December 8, 2005, Brown announced she had experienced severe and sudden hearing loss in both ears and she had not heard another person's voice in six months. Brown put <i>Black Roses</i> aside during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-Harris_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In June 2006, Brown said her hearing had been restored through surgery and she was planning to resume recording. Her label did not set a release date, but hoped the album would be out by the end of 2006. They were unsure if the title <i>Black Roses</i> would be kept.<sup id="cite_ref-deafness_cured_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deafness_cured-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In November 2006, there was speculation that Jay-Z was disappointed in Foxy Brown's "lack of productivity on the album" and was planning to drop her from the Def Jam label. The planned December 2006 release of <i>Black Roses</i> was cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-SOHH_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOHH-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 22, 2007, Black Hand Entertainment announced a management deal with Brown, with Chaz Williams as her manager. No release date was set for <i>Black Roses</i>, but Brown said the album was nearly complete.<sup id="cite_ref-SOHH2_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOHH2-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, a release date of September 6 was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-Mariel_Concepcion_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mariel_Concepcion-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On August 16, Black Hand Entertainment announced that Brown would leave Def Jam to launch an independent record label, Black Rose Entertainment, distributed by <a href="/wiki/Koch_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Koch Records">Koch Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Baller_Status_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baller_Status-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> A street album, <i><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn%27s_Don_Diva" title="Brooklyn&#39;s Don Diva">Brooklyn's Don Diva</a></i>, was eventually scheduled with a release date of December 4, but was delayed until the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Brooklyn's Don Diva</i> was ultimately released as a street album on May 13, 2008, after many delays triggered by her prison sentence. It contains two previously unreleased songs from her shelved album <i>Ill Na Na 2: The Fever.</i> The album peaked at No. 83 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, No. 8 on the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Albums" title="Independent Albums">Independent Albums</a> chart, and No. 5 on the <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2009.E2.80.932018:_Other_ventures"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009–2018:_Other_ventures">2009–2018: Other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2009–2018: Other ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2011, Brown released the diss track "Massacre",<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> a response to Lil' Kim's "Black Friday". On August 14, 2012, Foxy appeared as a special featured guest on <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Pink_Friday_Tour" title="Pink Friday Tour">Pink Friday Tour</a> in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-Universalmusic.com_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Universalmusic.com-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Rapper AZ later hinted in an interview that Brown was working on new material with Minaj.<sup id="cite_ref-Oct_22nd_2012_3:46PM_by_Nadine_Graham_Comments_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oct_22nd_2012_3:46PM_by_Nadine_Graham_Comments-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In August 2018, Brown made her first official guest appearance since 2009 on "Coco Chanel" from Nicki Minaj's fourth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_(Nicki_Minaj_album)" title="Queen (Nicki Minaj album)">Queen</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-highsnob_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highsnob-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2019.E2.80.93present:_Upcoming_fourth_studio_album"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–present:_Upcoming_fourth_studio_album">2019–present: Upcoming fourth studio album</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2019–present: Upcoming fourth studio album">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to media sources, Brown is back to work on her upcoming fourth studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-Winslow_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Winslow-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Madden_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Madden-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, Brown remixed <a href="/wiki/Casanova_(rapper)" title="Casanova (rapper)">Casanova</a>'s "So Brooklyn".<sup id="cite_ref-nevernaire.com_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nevernaire.com-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2020, Brown reunited with her group <a href="/wiki/The_Firm_(hip_hop_group)" title="The Firm (hip hop group)">The Firm</a> for the song "Full Circle" from Nas' album <i><a href="/wiki/King%27s_Disease" title="King&#39;s Disease">King's Disease</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Artistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

data-file-height="955" /></a></span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:173px;max-width:173px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Nas_in_Ottawa,_2007.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Nas_in_Ottawa%2C_2007.JPG/171px-Nas_in_Ottawa%2C_2007.JPG" decoding="async" width="171" height="203" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Nas_in_Ottawa%2C_2007.JPG/342px-Nas_in_Ottawa%2C_2007.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1839" data-file-height="2178" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Rappers <a href="/wiki/AZ_(rapper)" title="AZ (rapper)">AZ</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Nas_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nas (rapper)">Nas</a> (right) have supported Brown; the latter being one of Brown's major influences.</div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Musical style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Brown's lyrics have been described to be "raunchy" and "over-the-top" with "skimpy clothes to match."<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Her music is often centred around themes such as "fashion, sex, and the mafia" and is described as "intriguingly seductive" and having "a contemporary edge with a sleek and sexy soundscape."<sup id="cite_ref-FoxyUdiscover_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoxyUdiscover-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Her work for her debut album was described as "a heroine straight from the pages of a James Bond novel," selling over a million copies with the support of major male artists such as Nas and AZ.<sup id="cite_ref-FoxyUdiscover_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoxyUdiscover-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Brown's voice has been described as a "husky flow" with "dancehall swagger".<sup id="cite_ref-highsnob_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highsnob-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although her work was compared to rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim" title="Lil&#39; Kim">Lil' Kim</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Highsnobiety" title="Highsnobiety">Highsnobiety</a></i> writer David Opie said that,
</p>
<blockquote><p>Just because they were both the 'First Ladies' of their respective crews, doesn't mean that Foxy or Kim were identical by any means, and it was hugely misogynistic to suggest otherwise [...] In an industry that still actively mocks vulnerability and weakness, <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> needs more rappers who are willing to open up in this way, and the fact that Foxy did so such a long time ago speaks volumes about her artistry.<sup id="cite_ref-highsnob_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highsnob-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Brown's impact on the rap world has often been overlooked due to her legal run-ins, but it has been noted that "she's bright, talented, sexy and, most important, she's not afraid to take risks creatively" and that her "impact still stands."<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-highsnob_52-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highsnob-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Her albums have been cited to harness "a winning formula of looping R&amp;B songs into hip-hop hits, resulting in the genre-shifting record," <a href="/wiki/Ill_Na_Na" title="Ill Na Na">Ill Na Na</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The release of her album marked a monumental moment in hip-hop history, but was downplayed due to comparisons between her and rapper, Lil' Kim and although Foxy may not have achieved the "iconic status" Kim had reached, "her debut album was an essential part of a turning point in mainstream rap music."<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> author, <a href="/wiki/Kathy_Iandoli" title="Kathy Iandoli">Kathy Iandoli</a> stated,
</p>
<blockquote><p>In seeing Foxy ... release [<i><a href="/wiki/Ill_Na_Na" title="Ill Na Na">Ill Na Na</a></i>] it was a reassurance that skills paid off; it didn't really matter who was helping with the rhymes. It was the delivery and the content that was being said, and whose mouth it was coming out of. It was just a reassurance to me as a hip-hop head that this space might be opening up for women in a way that has never been done before. There was something about what [she] said and how [she was] saying it, that was hinting that a huge change was about to come.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Cited as a <a href="/wiki/Fashion_design" title="Fashion design">fashion icon</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Elle_(magazine)" title="Elle (magazine)">Elle</a></i> writer Janelle Harris wrote that Brown celebrated "the beauty of her mahogany skin as the self-professed 'dark-skinned Christian Dior poster girl,' boasted about being 'dripped in <a href="/wiki/Gabbana" class="mw-redirect" title="Gabbana">Gabbana</a> [...] starring in billboards as big as the pride of the Black girls who saw themselves in her likeness."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Described as one of the "illest to ever do it – regardless of gender," Scott Glaysher of <i><a href="/wiki/HipHopDX" title="HipHopDX">HipHopDX</a></i> noted that "If those aforementioned male rappers epitomize the menacing New York City mobster of the late 90s then Foxy represents the mob wife that is even more sinister with weaponized sexuality." He stated that "the sheer confidence and astute rhyming Foxy brought to <i><a href="/wiki/Ill_Na_Na" title="Ill Na Na">Ill Na Na</a></i>, makes it one of the 90s most memorable albums and a catalyst for the fierce feminine rap wave that followed.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> ranked her at 20, as one of the 30 Best Female Rappers Ever.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Brown's sophomore studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Chyna_Doll_(album)" title="Chyna Doll (album)">Chyna Doll</a></i> debuted at number one in 1999, making it only the second female rap album to debut at the top spot after <i><a href="/wiki/The_Miseducation_of_Lauryn_Hill" title="The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill">The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill</a></i> in 1998 by <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a> and eventually joined by <i><a href="/wiki/Let_There_Be_Eve...Ruff_Ryders%27_First_Lady" title="Let There Be Eve...Ruff Ryders&#39; First Lady">Let There Be Eve...Ruff Ryders' First Lady</a></i> in 1999 by <a href="/wiki/Eve_(rapper)" title="Eve (rapper)">Eve</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pink_Friday:_Roman_Reloaded" title="Pink Friday: Roman Reloaded">Pink Friday: Roman Reloaded</a></i> in 2012 by <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Privacy_(album)" title="Invasion of Privacy (album)">Invasion of Privacy</a></i> in 2018 by <a href="/wiki/Cardi_B" title="Cardi B">Cardi B</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ref1006723952_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref1006723952-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BB200_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BB200-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Her work has been paid homage to by numerous artists including, Nicki Minaj,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kash_Doll" title="Kash Doll">Kash Doll</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bia_(rapper)" title="Bia (rapper)">Bia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ivorian_Doll" title="Ivorian Doll">Ivorian Doll</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Megan_Thee_Stallion" title="Megan Thee Stallion">Megan Thee Stallion</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Maliibu_Miitch" title="Maliibu Miitch">Maliibu Miitch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Minaj has even gone so far to say that without Foxy she "may have never even started rapping" and that she is "the most influential female rapper."<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>From 1997 to 1999, she was engaged to fellow rapper, <a href="/wiki/Kurupt" title="Kurupt">Kurupt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, she announced that she was suffering from <a href="/wiki/Clinical_depression" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinical depression">depression</a>. She subsequently entered <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">drug rehabilitation</a> at Cornell University Medical College to receive treatment for <a href="/wiki/Opioid_addiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Opioid addiction">opioid addiction</a>, stating that she could no longer record or perform without resorting to <a href="/wiki/Morphine" title="Morphine">morphine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Salomon_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salomon-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Around 2001, she was engaged to Spragga Benz.<sup id="cite_ref-Spragga_Benz_allmusic_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spragga_Benz_allmusic-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Her uncle, Federico de la Asuncion, was one of 265 fatalities in the crash of <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines_Flight_587" title="American Airlines Flight 587">American Airlines Flight 587</a> on November 12, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Brown suffered <a href="/wiki/Hearing_loss" title="Hearing loss">hearing loss</a> from May 2005 to June 2006. She opted for a hearing aid, and, while recording music, had someone tap beats on her shoulder.<sup id="cite_ref-Harris_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-deafness_cured_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deafness_cured-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Brown denied reports claiming that she had made disparaging remarks about Jay-Z.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Combat_Jack" title="Combat Jack">Combat Jack</a>, she stated: "He never said not one bad thing about me. So when that false story came out about me talking about him, it's like, why would I say those things about him?"<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 13, 2017, she gave birth to her first child, a girl.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwateng-Clark_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwateng-Clark-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Comparisons between Brown and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Kim" class="mw-redirect" title="Lil Kim">Lil Kim</a> led to fierce competition.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> "Things got really personal when shots were fired outside a New York radio station."<sup id="cite_ref-CXFB_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CXFB-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The two have not resolved the issue, with Foxy siding and collaborating with rapper <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> in her feud with Kim in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-CXFB_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CXFB-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Following her release from prison, Kim does not acknowledge Brown. Brown, on the other hand, has consistently targeted Kim on a prime basis in her music and concerts since Kim's release.<sup id="cite_ref-youtube.com_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-XXLmag.com_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXLmag.com-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Starbury_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Starbury-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HipHopDX.com_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HipHopDX.com-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vibe.com_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vibe.com-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rap-Up.com_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rap-Up.com-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chandler_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Foxy_Brown.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Foxy_Brown.jpg/170px-Foxy_Brown.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="213" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Foxy_Brown.jpg/255px-Foxy_Brown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Foxy_Brown.jpg/340px-Foxy_Brown.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>2007 mug shot</figcaption></figure>
<p>Brown has a substantial history of assault and menacing.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
On September 7, 2007, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Criminal_Court" title="New York City Criminal Court">New York City Criminal Court</a> Judge Melissa Jackson sentenced Brown to one year in jail for violating her <a href="/wiki/Probation" title="Probation">probation</a> that stemmed from a fight in 2004 with two manicurists in a New York City <a href="/wiki/Nail_salon" title="Nail salon">nail salon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On September 12, representatives of the rapper disputed claims by her lawyer that she was pregnant.<sup id="cite_ref-Jailed_Foxy_Brown_&#39;not_pregnant&#39;_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jailed_Foxy_Brown_&#39;not_pregnant&#39;-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> On October 23, 2007, Brown was given 76 days in <a href="/wiki/Solitary_confinement" title="Solitary confinement">solitary confinement</a> due to a physical altercation that took place on October 3, with another prisoner. According to the prison authorities, Brown, the next day after the incident, was also verbally abusive toward correction officers and refused to take a random drug test.<sup id="cite_ref-Scharm_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scharm-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Prison authorities reported on November 27 that she was released "from solitary confinement...for good behavior",<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and Brown was finally released from prison on April 18, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-McGee_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGee-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 22, 2010, Brown was arrested and charged with one count of <a href="/wiki/Criminal_contempt" class="mw-redirect" title="Criminal contempt">criminal contempt</a>, which is a class E felony (the least severe), for violating an <a href="/wiki/Order_of_protection" class="mw-redirect" title="Order of protection">order of protection</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard.com_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard.com-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The charge stems from an incident during the evening of July 21, 2010, in which it was claimed that Brown swore at, then <a href="/wiki/Mooned" class="mw-redirect" title="Mooned">mooned</a> her neighbor Arlene Raymond, at whom she had thrown her BlackBerry, in 2007. Following the BlackBerry incident, Raymond sought and received a restraining order against Brown. Following her arrest, Brown appeared in court where she pleaded "not guilty" to the charge and was released on a $5,000 bail. If convicted, she faced up to seven years' imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-Nydailynews.com_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nydailynews.com-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> On July 12, 2011, the charges were dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-Gorta_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gorta-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Foxy_Brown_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">An arrest report by the <a href="/wiki/Broward_County_Sheriff%27s_Office" title="Broward County Sheriff&#39;s Office">Broward County Sheriff's Office</a> dated February 16, 2007, listed her birth year as 1978. An article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> from September 8, 2007, stated: "Ms. Brown, who turned 29 on Thursday [September 6], had tried to conceal her identity by writing her name as Enga rather than Inga, and giving her date of birth as 1980 rather than 1978." The website <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> lists her birth date as September 6, 1979. An <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> article from March 9, 2001, appears to support the 1979 birth year. In her song "I Don't Need Nobody", Marchand raps "1978 / The year I was born".<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Indicates the year of ceremony. Each year is linked to the article about the awards held that year, wherever possible.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
